## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is a reaction rate expressed as a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard object of chemical kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are kinetic rate laws (zero/first/second/nth order), reversible relaxation toward equilibrium, and empirical time-dependent rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited or saturated regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A+A type effective law)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order)
- Constant source/sink with first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (production plus linear degradation; driven system)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible first-order (implicit B via conservation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (A ⇌ B with total c2 conserved)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplification with finite capacity c1)
- Inhibited/limited rate (rational): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective saturation/inhibition at high A without explicit other species)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (aging/catalyst deactivation or ramped conditions)
- Exponentially varying rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (time-dependent activity/temperature protocol folded into k(t))
- Mixed-order (sum of pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order loss channels)
- Shifted-power driving force: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1)**c2 (nonlinear relaxation toward equilibrium c1)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Net consumption of A typically implies dA_dt < 0 and monotone decay; forms proportional to A or A**n preserve the sign for A > 0.
- Reaction order identification: linear dependence on A suggests first-order; quadratic suggests second-order; A**c1 supports fractional/empirical orders.
- Approach to a nonzero steady state is indicated by a factor (A - c1); the steady state occurs where dA_dt = 0 at A = c1.
- Reversible/relaxation kinetics often decompose into forward minus backward terms, e.g., -c0*A + (backward term), yielding equilibrium when terms balance.
- Autocatalysis produces initial acceleration (rate increases with A) and later slowdown as A approaches a limit (c1 - A factor).
- Multiple pathways appear as additive loss terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2), with dominance switching across concentration ranges.
- Time-dependent operating conditions (temperature programs, catalyst decay) can be absorbed into k(t), giving explicit t in dA_dt via (c0 + c1*t) or exp(-c1*t).
- Rational forms like A/(1 + c1*A) encode diminishing returns at high A (effective inhibition/transport limitation) while remaining approximately linear at low A.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK6)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.4466*A*exp(-0.08660*t) + 0.9910*sin(sqrt(A))`

The GT has two fundamentally different basis functions:
1. `A*exp(-αt)` — a product of A and a decaying exponential in t
2. `sin(sqrt(A))` — a sine of the square root of A

Let me examine what basis functions each candidate offers.

**Key observation:** The GT contains `sin(sqrt(A))`, which is a very specific nonlinear function of A. None of the candidates contain `sin(...)` except **Candidate 4**, which has `sin(A*c3 + c4)`. Let me check if `sin(A*c3 + c4)` can equal `sin(sqrt(A))` — this would require `A*c3 + c4 = sqrt(A) + 2πn` for all A, which is impossible since `A*c3 + c4` is linear in A while `sqrt(A)` is not.

The GT also contains `A*exp(-αt)`, which couples A and t multiplicatively. Most candidates have terms that are either purely functions of A or purely functions of t, or have specific coupling structures like `A/(c+t)²`, `A*t/(...)`, etc.

Let me check if any candidate has both:
- A term that can represent `A*exp(ct)` (the A-t coupling)
- A term that can represent `sin(sqrt(A))`

**No candidate contains `sin(sqrt(A))` or any `sin` function except Candidate 4**, which has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` — linear argument, not `sqrt(A)`.

Since `sin(sqrt(A))` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of:
- Polynomials in A (`A², A, 1`)
- `exp(cA)` terms
- `log(cA+1)` terms
- `A^c` power terms
- `1/(A+c)²` terms
- Any functions of t alone

...none of these basis functions can reproduce `sin(sqrt(A))`. These are all linearly independent function classes.

Let me verify each candidate systematically — they all use combinations of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, and rational functions of A and t. None contain `sin(sqrt(A))` or anything that could reduce to it.

Even Candidate 4 with `sin(A*c3 + c4)` cannot match because `sin(A*c3 + c4) ≠ sin(sqrt(A))` for all A.

Candidates with `A^c` terms (13, 20, 27, 31, 39, 46): Setting `c = 0.5` gives `sqrt(A)`, but `c*sqrt(A) ≠ sin(sqrt(A))` for all A.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT**.
